"text":"Reposting via @anchoragemuseum \ud83e\udde1Join our current artist-in-residence @melissachimera this Saturday
 Oct. 1
 from 11 a.m. to 3 p.m. at the UAA Arts Building to celebrate the start of Filipino-American Heritage Month.\n\nA Honolulu native of Lebanese and Filipino ancestry
 Chimera is visiting Alaska to expand her research related to the Pacific-wide Filipinx diaspora. She will speak at 2:30 p.m. about \"Immigration and Art: Opportunities and Challenges
\" focusing on her family's history as immigrants from Lebanon and the Philippines
 as well as the recent work exploring the journeys of today's Filipinx immigrants who inhabit the literal and imagined liminal spaces between nations.\n\nPhoto courtesy of Dino Morrow Photography and Above the Equator Gallery."

"text":"Reposting via @anchoragemuseum \ud83e\udde1Join our current artist-in-residence @melissachimera this Saturday
 Oct. 1
 from 11 a.m. to 3 p.m. at the UAA Arts Building to celebrate the start of Filipino-American Heritage Month.\n\nA Honolulu native of Lebanese and Filipino ancestry
 Chimera is visiting Alaska to expand her research related to the Pacific-wide Filipinx diaspora. She will speak at 2:30 p.m. about \"Immigration and Art: Opportunities and Challenges
\" focusing on her family's history as immigrants from Lebanon and the Philippines
 as well as the recent work exploring the journeys of today's Filipinx immigrants who inhabit the literal and imagined liminal spaces between nations.\n\nPhoto courtesy of Dino Morrow Photography and Above the Equator Gallery."

"text":"Reposting via @anchoragemuseum \ud83e\udde1Join our current artist-in-residence @melissachimera this Saturday
 Oct. 1
 from 11 a.m. to 3 p.m. at the UAA Arts Building to celebrate the start of Filipino-American Heritage Month.\n\nA Honolulu native of Lebanese and Filipino ancestry
 Chimera is visiting Alaska to expand her research related to the Pacific-wide Filipinx diaspora. She will speak at 2:30 p.m. about \"Immigration and Art: Opportunities and Challenges
\" focusing on her family's history as immigrants from Lebanon and the Philippines
 as well as the recent work exploring the journeys of today's Filipinx immigrants who inhabit the literal and imagined liminal spaces between nations.\n\nPhoto courtesy of Dino Morrow Photography and Above the Equator Gallery."

 from 11 a.m. to 3 p.m. at the UAA Arts Building to celebrate the start of Filipino-American Heritage Month.\n\nA Honolulu native of Lebanese and Filipino ancestry
 Chimera is visiting Alaska to expand her research related to the Pacific-wide Filipinx diaspora. She will speak at 2:30 p.m. about \"Immigration and Art: Opportunities and Challenges

 as well as the recent work exploring the journeys of today's Filipinx immigrants who inhabit the literal and imagined liminal spaces between nations.\n\nPhoto courtesy of Dino Morrow Photography and Above the Equator Gallery."

"text":"Reposting via @anchoragemuseum \ud83e\udde1Join our current artist-in-residence @melissachimera this Saturday
 Oct. 1
 from 11 a.m. to 3 p.m. at the UAA Arts Building to celebrate the start of Filipino-American Heritage Month.\n\nA Honolulu native of Lebanese and Filipino ancestry
 Chimera is visiting Alaska to expand her research related to the Pacific-wide Filipinx diaspora. She will speak at 2:30 p.m. about \"Immigration and Art: Opportunities and Challenges
\" focusing on her family's history as immigrants from Lebanon and the Philippines
 as well as the recent work exploring the journeys of today's Filipinx immigrants who inhabit the literal and imagined liminal spaces between nations.\n\nPhoto courtesy of Dino Morrow Photography and Above the Equator Gallery."

"text":"Reposting via @anchoragemuseum \ud83e\udde1Join our current artist-in-residence @melissachimera this Saturday
 Oct. 1
 from 11 a.m. to 3 p.m. at the UAA Arts Building to celebrate the start of Filipino-American Heritage Month.\n\nA Honolulu native of Lebanese and Filipino ancestry
 Chimera is visiting Alaska to expand her research related to the Pacific-wide Filipinx diaspora. She will speak at 2:30 p.m. about \"Immigration and Art: Opportunities and Challenges
\" focusing on her family's history as immigrants from Lebanon and the Philippines
 as well as the recent work exploring the journeys of today's Filipinx immigrants who inhabit the literal and imagined liminal spaces between nations.\n\nPhoto courtesy of Dino Morrow Photography and Above the Equator Gallery."

"text":"Reposting via @anchoragemuseum \ud83e\udde1Join our current artist-in-residence @melissachimera this Saturday
 Oct. 1
 from 11 a.m. to 3 p.m. at the UAA Arts Building to celebrate the start of Filipino-American Heritage Month.\n\nA Honolulu native of Lebanese and Filipino ancestry
 Chimera is visiting Alaska to expand her research related to the Pacific-wide Filipinx diaspora. She will speak at 2:30 p.m. about \"Immigration and Art: Opportunities and Challenges
\" focusing on her family's history as immigrants from Lebanon and the Philippines
 as well as the recent work exploring the journeys of today's Filipinx immigrants who inhabit the literal and imagined liminal spaces between nations.\n\nPhoto courtesy of Dino Morrow Photography and Above the Equator Gallery."

"text":"Reposting via @anchoragemuseum \ud83e\udde1Join our current artist-in-residence @melissachimera this Saturday
 Oct. 1
 from 11 a.m. to 3 p.m. at the UAA Arts Building to celebrate the start of Filipino-American Heritage Month.\n\nA Honolulu native of Lebanese and Filipino ancestry
 Chimera is visiting Alaska to expand her research related to the Pacific-wide Filipinx diaspora. She will speak at 2:30 p.m. about \"Immigration and Art: Opportunities and Challenges
\" focusing on her family's history as immigrants from Lebanon and the Philippines
 as well as the recent work exploring the journeys of today's Filipinx immigrants who inhabit the literal and imagined liminal spaces between nations.\n\nPhoto courtesy of Dino Morrow Photography and Above the Equator Gallery."

 from 11 a.m. to 3 p.m. at the UAA Arts Building to celebrate the start of Filipino-American Heritage Month.\n\nA Honolulu native of Lebanese and Filipino ancestry
 Chimera is visiting Alaska to expand her research related to the Pacific-wide Filipinx diaspora. She will speak at 2:30 p.m. about \"Immigration and Art: Opportunities and Challenges
\" focusing on her family's history as immigrants from Lebanon and the Philippines
 as well as the recent work exploring the journeys of today's Filipinx immigrants who inhabit the literal and imagined liminal spaces between nations.\n\nPhoto courtesy of Dino Morrow Photography and Above the Equator Gallery."

 Oct. 1

 Chimera is visiting Alaska to expand her research related to the Pacific-wide Filipinx diaspora. She will speak at 2:30 p.m. about \"Immigration and Art: Opportunities and Challenges
\" focusing on her family's history as immigrants from Lebanon and the Philippines
 as well as the recent work exploring the journeys of today's Filipinx immigrants who inhabit the literal and imagined liminal spaces between nations.\n\nPhoto courtesy of Dino Morrow Photography and Above the Equator Gallery."

"text":"Reposting via @anchoragemuseum \ud83e\udde1Join our current artist-in-residence @melissachimera this Saturday
 Oct. 1
 from 11 a.m. to 3 p.m. at the UAA Arts Building to celebrate the start of Filipino-American Heritage Month.\n\nA Honolulu native of Lebanese and Filipino ancestry
 Chimera is visiting Alaska to expand her research related to the Pacific-wide Filipinx diaspora. She will speak at 2:30 p.m. about \"Immigration and Art: Opportunities and Challenges
\" focusing on her family's history as immigrants from Lebanon and the Philippines
 as well as the recent work exploring the journeys of today's Filipinx immigrants who inhabit the literal and imagined liminal spaces between nations.\n\nPhoto courtesy of Dino Morrow Photography and Above the Equator Gallery."

"text":"Reposting via @anchoragemuseum \ud83e\udde1Join our current artist-in-residence @melissachimera this Saturday
 Oct. 1
 from 11 a.m. to 3 p.m. at the UAA Arts Building to celebrate the start of Filipino-American Heritage Month.\n\nA Honolulu native of Lebanese and Filipino ancestry
 Chimera is visiting Alaska to expand her research related to the Pacific-wide Filipinx diaspora. She will speak at 2:30 p.m. about \"Immigration and Art: Opportunities and Challenges
\" focusing on her family's history as immigrants from Lebanon and the Philippines
 as well as the recent work exploring the journeys of today's Filipinx immigrants who inhabit the literal and imagined liminal spaces between nations.\n\nPhoto courtesy of Dino Morrow Photography and Above the Equator Gallery."

"text":"Reposting via @anchoragemuseum \ud83e\udde1Join our current artist-in-residence @melissachimera this Saturday
 Oct. 1
 from 11 a.m. to 3 p.m. at the UAA Arts Building to celebrate the start of Filipino-American Heritage Month.\n\nA Honolulu native of Lebanese and Filipino ancestry
 Chimera is visiting Alaska to expand her research related to the Pacific-wide Filipinx diaspora. She will speak at 2:30 p.m. about \"Immigration and Art: Opportunities and Challenges
\" focusing on her family's history as immigrants from Lebanon and the Philippines
 as well as the recent work exploring the journeys of today's Filipinx immigrants who inhabit the literal and imagined liminal spaces between nations.\n\nPhoto courtesy of Dino Morrow Photography and Above the Equator Gallery."

"text":"Reposting via @anchoragemuseum \ud83e\udde1Join our current artist-in-residence @melissachimera this Saturday
 Oct. 1
 from 11 a.m. to 3 p.m. at the UAA Arts Building to celebrate the start of Filipino-American Heritage Month.\n\nA Honolulu native of Lebanese and Filipino ancestry
 Chimera is visiting Alaska to expand her research related to the Pacific-wide Filipinx diaspora. She will speak at 2:30 p.m. about \"Immigration and Art: Opportunities and Challenges
\" focusing on her family's history as immigrants from Lebanon and the Philippines
 as well as the recent work exploring the journeys of today's Filipinx immigrants who inhabit the literal and imagined liminal spaces between nations.\n\nPhoto courtesy of Dino Morrow Photography and Above the Equator Gallery."

 Chimera is visiting Alaska to expand her research related to the Pacific-wide Filipinx diaspora. She will speak at 2:30 p.m. about \"Immigration and Art: Opportunities and Challenges
\" focusing on her family's history as immigrants from Lebanon and the Philippines
 as well as the recent work exploring the journeys of today's Filipinx immigrants who inhabit the literal and imagined liminal spaces between nations.\n\nPhoto courtesy of Dino Morrow Photography and Above the Equator Gallery."

 Chimera is visiting Alaska to expand her research related to the Pacific-wide Filipinx diaspora. She will speak at 2:30 p.m. about \"Immigration and Art: Opportunities and Challenges
\" focusing on her family's history as immigrants from Lebanon and the Philippines
 as well as the recent work exploring the journeys of today's Filipinx immigrants who inhabit the literal and imagined liminal spaces between nations.\n\nPhoto courtesy of Dino Morrow Photography and Above the Equator Gallery."

"text":"Reposting via @anchoragemuseum \ud83e\udde1Join our current artist-in-residence @melissachimera this Saturday
 Oct. 1
 from 11 a.m. to 3 p.m. at the UAA Arts Building to celebrate the start of Filipino-American Heritage Month.\n\nA Honolulu native of Lebanese and Filipino ancestry
 Chimera is visiting Alaska to expand her research related to the Pacific-wide Filipinx diaspora. She will speak at 2:30 p.m. about \"Immigration and Art: Opportunities and Challenges
\" focusing on her family's history as immigrants from Lebanon and the Philippines
 as well as the recent work exploring the journeys of today's Filipinx immigrants who inhabit the literal and imagined liminal spaces between nations.\n\nPhoto courtesy of Dino Morrow Photography and Above the Equator Gallery."

"text":"Reposting via @anchoragemuseum \ud83e\udde1Join our current artist-in-residence @melissachimera this Saturday
 Oct. 1
 from 11 a.m. to 3 p.m. at the UAA Arts Building to celebrate the start of Filipino-American Heritage Month.\n\nA Honolulu native of Lebanese and Filipino ancestry
 Chimera is visiting Alaska to expand her research related to the Pacific-wide Filipinx diaspora. She will speak at 2:30 p.m. about \"Immigration and Art: Opportunities and Challenges
\" focusing on her family's history as immigrants from Lebanon and the Philippines
 as well as the recent work exploring the journeys of today's Filipinx immigrants who inhabit the literal and imagined liminal spaces between nations.\n\nPhoto courtesy of Dino Morrow Photography and Above the Equator Gallery."
